New Developments in North China: The United States Cannot Stand Idly By; Existing Treaties Should Be Strictly Respected; The Hull Declaration is Clearly Directed at Japan; The British Foreign Secretary's Words Express Concern 4

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull issued a formal statement today, declaring to the world that the United States cannot turn a blind eye to the autonomy movement in North China and requesting that all nations respect existing treaties. Although Japan was not mentioned in the statement, it is clearly aimed at Japan. Hull stated that regardless of the origin or instigator, it is a fact that someone is attempting to make significant changes to the political status and situation of several northern provinces of China, and that this is being resisted by China. Any unusual development in any part of China is naturally of concern not only to the people of China and the United States, but also to the people of all countries with interests in China, as their relationship with China and their rights and obligations under treaties are similar. The interests of the United States in North China are the same as those of other countries. Therefore, the US government is closely monitoring the developments in North China. In this period of global political unrest and economic instability, governments and peoples of all countries must adhere to principles and promises, he said. In response to questions from reporters, the State Department clarified that the aforementioned statement was directed at Japan. At the same time, rumors of Anglo-American cooperation regarding North China have not yet been confirmed. (Reuters dispatch of the 6th)

(London) Chinese Ambassador Guo Taiqi, when interviewed by a Reuters correspondent today, welcomed Secretary of State Hull's declaration regarding North China, saying that it proves that the United States has abandoned its nearly isolationist stance. Ambassador Guo also mentioned the statement by the spokesperson of the Japanese Foreign Ministry in Tokyo that the Nine-Power Treaty does not apply to the North China dispute, saying that this proves the difficulties China faces in dealing with Japan. Sir Austen Chamberlain, in a previous speech in the House of Commons, urged China to adopt a realistic view and compromise with Japan regarding Manchuria. He is more realistic in his views of China than anyone else. China has been slow to compromise with Japan because it firmly believes that no compromise can be reached or that Japan's demands will ever cease. (Reuters dispatch of the 6th)

Hull Declaration Full Text

(Nanjing) U.S. Secretary of State Hull issued a statement to the American press on the 5th regarding the North China incident. We have obtained the full text from relevant sources and translated it as follows: Political disputes of an extraordinary nature and with far-reaching implications are currently occurring in northern China. According to reports, these changes involve many people, are happening very quickly, cover a wide range, and opinions are very divided. No one can predict what the future holds. But regardless of the origin, instigator, or method, it is a fact that someone is working to make significant changes to the political status and situation of several northern provinces of China, and that this is being resisted. Any unusual change in any part of China is naturally and necessarily of concern not only to the government and people of China, but also to all countries enjoying interests in China, as their relationship with China and their treaty rights and obligations within China are largely the same. The United States is one such country. In the region in question, the interests of the United States are the same as those of other countries. In this region, the United States has a large number of expatriates, some property, and important commercial and cultural enterprises. Therefore, the United States government is paying close attention to the changes in the situation. Political unrest and pressure can cause anxiety and fear, and can also lead to economic and social unrest, making it difficult to enjoy treaty rights and fulfill treaty obligations. The views of the United States government on such events, whether they relate to China or the world, are well known to the world. In this time of global political unrest and economic instability, in the view of our country (referring to the United States) government, it is most important for the governments and peoples of all countries to keep faith and promises. I have repeatedly said that in international relations, there must be faith and promises must be kept so that we can have a sense of credibility, stability, and security, as these are necessary for orderly life and progress. Our government has unwavering faith in the fundamental principles of its long-standing policies, and our government adheres firmly to the provisions of the treaties it has acceded to, and continues to expect that all countries will respect the terms of the treaties they have solemnly signed, as these terms facilitate and adjust the relationship between the signatory countries in order to obtain mutual and common benefits. (Central News Agency dispatch of the 6th)

British Parliament Foreign Affairs Debate

(London) During the debate on foreign affairs in the House of Commons last night, Foreign Secretary Hoare spoke, expressing concern about the serious situation in North China, saying that the Chinese sky is covered in dense haze, referring to the so-called North China autonomy movement. News of Japanese personnel activities is frequently reported. Recent Japanese military actions are probably related to the Japanese personnel movement. This news has caused great concern to the British government, so it has specifically instructed its chargé d'affaires in Tokyo to notify the government with great attention, and declared that we welcome Japan to make a frank announcement of its policies. The Japanese government told the British chargé d'affaires that the autonomy movement is purely a Chinese movement. The Japanese government is closely watching this matter because it has extensive interests in North China. Some say that Japan is implementing military intervention, but this is unfounded. Japanese troops have not been transferred into China as a result of the autonomy movement. The troops stationed in Tianjin and Beijing are lower than the original number. The movement of troops near Beijing is the movement of troops originally stationed south of the Great Wall. Japan has the inherent right to maintain troops there. The reported movement of trains is for this reason. The Foreign Secretary continued that the overall situation is very chaotic, but he believes that the talks currently underway between the Chinese and Japanese governments will certainly enable any current difficulties to be resolved peacefully. He considers the recurrence of such incidents to be unfortunate, as regardless of their true nature, they are sufficient to make people believe that Japan is currently using its influence to shape the development and administrative arrangements of China's internal affairs. Any event that gives rise to this belief can only damage Japan's reputation and hinder the development of mutually friendly relations between Japan and China and its other neighbors that all parties desire. The Foreign Secretary then mentioned the mission of Sir Frederick Leith-Ross, the British government's economic advisor, to the Far East, saying that China's finances are becoming increasingly difficult and its currency system is becoming increasingly chaotic, which is harmful to China and the business community. It seems necessary to find a remedy. The British government's intention is that the Chinese government cannot satisfactorily resolve all of its difficulties unless it obtains the friendly cooperation of the countries concerned, together with China itself. Based on this view, we decided to send Sir Frederick Leith-Ross to the Far East to conduct an investigation, while other governments did not accept our suggestion to take similar action. Sir Frederick Leith-Ross went to Shanghai to consult with the Chinese authorities and began his investigation after staying in Tokyo for several weeks. While discussions were underway, the Chinese government was forced to take swift action due to a sudden exchange rate crisis in the country, and announced a change in the legal basis of the silver currency on November 4. The Foreign Secretary then solemnly declared that the Chinese government's action was entirely voluntary and did not seek the opinion of Sir Frederick Leith-Ross. All reports received by the British government to date indicate that the currency reform plan has been welcomed in all quarters and has had a good effect in restoring confidence. (Reuters dispatch of the 6th)

(London) Conservative MP Stratton asked Foreign Secretary Hoare in the House of Commons, "Given that Japan is continuing to occupy China with armed forces, what steps will the British government take to protect British commercial interests in China?" Foreign Secretary Hoare immediately replied in writing, stating, "The governments of China and Japan are fully aware of the attitude taken by the British government to protect British interests in China. As for the current situation in China, especially the situation in North China, the British Ambassador to China will closely monitor it. But so far, the British government has no need to take any special steps regarding the situation Mr. Stratton is concerned about." (Havas dispatch of the 5th)

Number of Japanese Troops Stationed in Tianjin Suddenly Increases 5

The total number of troops has exceeded the number stipulated in the Boxer Protocol. All countries are paying close attention. (Special dispatch of the 6th)

Commentary

The Current Sino-Japanese Problem 11

— Ran

In a world where nations stand side by side, every nation cherishes its own country. If a country is subjected to aggression by a strong power, the patriotic sentiments of its people will inevitably be very high, leading to patriotic actions to resist foreign aggression. At this time, even if the ruler of the country wants to temporarily tolerate foreign aggression, he must show his determination to uphold the national stand in order to gain the understanding and sympathy of the people. This simple common sense can also be used to explain the current Sino-Japanese problem.

China and Japan stand side by side in East Asia. They are truly said to be of the same script and race, with a relationship of interdependence. Unfortunately, the modern civilizations of the two countries have not developed equally, and there is a difference between advanced and backward. More unfortunately, due to the limitations of the world situation, the advanced country, due to its development needs, not only cannot support the backward country, but also wants to use the backward country as its sacrifice. On the other hand, the backward China, under the situation of being cut up, has no choice but to struggle for survival. This is why the Sino-Japanese relationship has deteriorated since the Republic of China. Recently, the global economic panic has intensified the colonial competition among the great powers. Japan, in order to expand its colonial territories, actually wants to open up a path of Sino-Japanese friendship under the threat of force. This kind of friendship is no different from the friendship between a wolf and a lamb. How can our nation accept it?

Our nation today still has only struggle left. The purpose of struggle is only to seek survival. Whoever does not allow us to survive, we should recognize as an enemy. The Japanese often express anger at our country's approach to Europe and the United States. In fact, since they have placed our nation in a state of struggle, we have no choice but to seek help in our urgency. Japan, if it wants to seek genuine friendship with us, this friendship must be built on the basis of "mutual coexistence." For this, Japan must first abandon its past aggressive attitude, and especially respect the most ordinary and basic public opinion of our nation, namely

"Cherish our own country."

Public opinion is irresistible. This is not only something that people in neighboring countries should understand, but also something that our country's authorities should understand. "Those who follow it will prosper, and those who oppose it will perish" is indeed shown by history. Why did the Northern Warlords fall? Why did the National Revolution progress? Why are politicians and military men who are willing to betray the country always despised by the people? The reason is very obvious. The more serious the national crisis, the greater the power of public opinion. Those in power, if they want to overcome the current difficulties, have no choice but to comply with public opinion.

British and French Experts' Proposals Fail to Satisfy Italy's Desires; British and French Foreign Ministers to Meet in Paris Today; Awaiting Agreement Before Submitting to the League of Nations 12

(Rome) Diplomats here today generally believe that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini is preparing to reject the Anglo-French proposals for resolving the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. It is believed that the agreement is unsatisfactory because it fails to meet Italy's minimum territorial expansion demands. But Mussolini is prepared to compromise, so he will not flatly reject the plan, but will hint that he is willing to accept a more generous proposal. (Guomin News Agency dispatch of the 5th)

(London) According to official sources, the solution to the Italo-Ethiopian dispute currently being discussed by the British and French governments, after the two countries have fully agreed, will probably be submitted to the League of Nations first, or temporarily kept by the foreign ministries of the United Kingdom and France. It is not intended to be submitted to Italy immediately before Italy's attitude changes, as there seems to be little hope for Italy to change its attitude in the short term. (Havas dispatch of the 6th)

(Paris) According to "Le Temps," British Foreign Office expert on Abyssinia, Henderson, and French Foreign Office Director for African Affairs, Saint-Quentin, recently reached a consensus in their discussions here, which could serve as the basis for resolving the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. This proposal was personally delivered to the Italian Ambassador to France, Cerutti, by Prime Minister Laval yesterday. The newspaper also said that Britain is expected to propose a ceasefire based on the above plan to both sides on the 12th of this month. (Havas dispatch of the 5th)

(Paris) It is heard that Prime Minister Laval explained to the Italian Ambassador to France, Cerutti, last night that Britain and France are responsible for resolving the Italo-Ethiopian dispute, so they hope that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini will explain his minimum requirements for Abyssinia. It is also the general impression that Prime Minister Laval and British Foreign Secretary Hoare are now eager for Italy to respond before the meeting of the Committee of Eighteen on December 12. As for the plan drafted by the British and French experts, in general, it involves the exchange of land between Italy and Ethiopia without harming the sovereignty of either party. However, according to informed sources, the two experts have not been able to fully agree on some points. (Havas dispatch of the 5th)

(London) Semi-official circles here still doubt whether the future negotiations with Italy will be successful, because it is reported that the result of the Italian Ambassador Grandi's visit to the Foreign Office yesterday did not reveal any new factors to fulfill the expectations of the general public. It is generally believed that even if Italy accepts the Anglo-French proposal as the basis for starting negotiations, a compromise may not be reached before January next year, because by January, the two rainy seasons of Ethiopia will be approaching, and economic sanctions will definitely begin to have a serious impact at that time. When Italian public opinion feels this difficulty, it may be easier to accept a peaceful resolution of the dispute. (Havas dispatch of the 5th)

Key Points of British and French Experts' Proposals

(Paris) According to "Le Temps," the key points of the British and French experts' proposals are as follows: (1) Italy would demarcate a corridor in Eritrea, along with the port of Assab, and cede it to Ethiopia to build a railway from the port to the Ethiopian capital. (2) The existing borders of Ethiopia would be modified, with part of the northern Tigray province ceded to Italy, but the holy city of Aksum would remain Ethiopian. (3) The entire southern Ogaden province and its western areas up to 40 degrees east longitude would be ceded to Italy, as well as the eastern Danakil region and the Wasa region and part of the Harar province, so that Italy could connect its Eritrean and Somaliland territories. (4) The above agreement should take the form of an Italo-Ethiopian treaty. (5) The sovereignty of the remaining parts of Ethiopia would remain with the Ethiopian Emperor, and the Emperor could request assistance from the League of Nations, but it would not be necessary to request assistance from the League of Nations as previously suggested. (Havas dispatch of the 5th)

Rome's Attitude is Very Cold

(Rome) Since the news that British and French experts were in Paris to hold talks and had reached an agreement that could serve as the basis for resolving the Italo-Ethiopian dispute, the general sentiment here had indeed gradually eased, but it was very temporary, and after only three days it returned to coldness. Although British Foreign Secretary Hoare delivered a foreign policy speech in the British House of Commons last night, explaining Britain's attitude towards the Italo-Ethiopian dispute, according to what this agency's diplomatic correspondent knows, the cold emotions here have not changed due to Hoare's remarks. Diplomatic circles believe that a concrete plan for resolving the Italo-Ethiopian problem has not yet been formed, which contradicts what was expected a few days ago, so the future of the problem looks even worse. Responsible parties also said that although the various guarantees provided by Hoare to Italy are welcome, their content has long been known to the country. This shows that the British attitude has not changed from beginning to end. It is generally believed that Hoare's speech almost indicated that the necessary condition for starting any negotiations is to first stop the war, which the Italian government believes there is no room to accept. (Havas dispatch of the 6th)

Hoare Departs for France This Morning

(London) According to responsible sources, Foreign Secretary Sir Samuel Hoare will be accompanied by Parliamentary Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs Vansittart when he goes to Paris. Vansittart will stay in the French capital for several days to discuss with the French authorities the possibility of negotiating with Germany on the limitation of land and air armaments. Foreign Secretary Hoare is now scheduled to depart for France on Saturday morning and, after talking with Prime Minister Laval in Paris, will go to Switzerland for a few days of rest that evening. (Havas dispatch of the 5th)

Italian Air Force Bombs Taxis City: Three Attacks Result in Heavy Casualties; King Remains Calm Despite Scare; Decisive Battle Imminent 13

(Paris) According to an urgent dispatch from the capital of Albania, nine Italian aircraft attacked Taxis City today, where the Albanian King resides. The King and his accompanying young son were unharmed. Bombs hit the palace of Crown Prince Hassan, causing a portion of it to be destroyed by fire. The Crown Prince is currently stationed in the capital as regent for military and political affairs. American Hospital was also hit by bombs, destroying several hospital tents. Italian aircraft carried out a total of three attacks. It is reported that a total of thirty-two people were killed and two hundred injured, with varying degrees of severity. Among the injured was an officer from the Inspection Office who sustained minor injuries. After the attacks, the King and his young son immediately went to the American Hospital to visit the wounded. The three attacks caused significant material losses. The Albanian government is planning to lodge a serious protest with the League of Nations due to the Italian aircraft bombing an undefended town and a hospital displaying the Red Cross flag. Today, Italian aircraft were active elsewhere, bombing Albanian troops engaged in combat, resulting in numerous casualties. Gonda Town was also bombed last night. It is reported that the Albanian King, although startled today, remained calm and will soon go to the front lines to consult with various commanders regarding future Albanian military strategy. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Taxis City: A special correspondent of this newspaper, Lavoya, reports: Ten Italian aircraft flew over this area at 8:30 this morning, carrying out indiscriminate bombing. (It is noted that the Albanian King is currently stationed in Taxis City, directing military operations at the front.) Subsequently, twenty more Italian aircraft flew over the city. It is rumored that one Italian plane was shot down by Albanian forces. The targets of the Italian bombing were the Crown Prince's palace and the American Hospital in the city. A portion of the Crown Prince's palace has been destroyed. It is reported that ten people were killed and eighty seriously injured. The Albanian government has lodged a protest against the Italian aircraft bombing the undefended Taxis City and the hospital displaying the Red Cross flag. The Albanian King personally visited the American Hospital to visit the wounded. It is reported that Italian aircraft also flew to Gonda Town yesterday afternoon and dropped bombs. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Albanian Capital: This newspaper's special correspondent, O'Chana, reports: Since the Italian Air Force bombed Taxis City this morning, military personnel here believe that a major war between the Italian and Albanian armies will begin soon. It is especially believed that the Italian aircraft simultaneously bombed Qiqi Jia City on the Southern Wojiaden front, making the possibility of a decisive battle even more credible. It is generally believed that the Italian aircraft's target was to bomb the Albanian Emperor, because if the Albanian Emperor were to be lost, internal difficulties would inevitably arise in Albania. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(London) According to a dispatch from Taxis to the Chronicle, the Albanian Emperor has ordered preparations for an attack on Italian forces in the north, vowing to drive them out of the country. This order was issued to all Albanian troops currently attacking Magar. Before issuing the order at midnight, the Albanian Emperor convened a military meeting and had long telephone conversations with front-line generals. The Albanian Emperor has erected a red tent in Taxis today, which is a signal of offensive operations. Government inspectors are unwilling to disclose the date and location of the battle but said that the Albanian Emperor will personally go to the front lines to command 600,000 troops. (National Telegram, 5th)

Asmara: Today's public report states that an Albanian team attacked the Italian army's supply train behind the lines, northwest of Jiagaer, killing only one Italian soldier and wounding two. Italian aircraft bombed a column of Albanian soldiers with bombs and machine guns in Huqila, twenty miles north of Gonda, causing many Albanian casualties, and they dispersed immediately. Yesterday and today, a large squadron of Italian bombers, accompanied by many reconnaissance aircraft, bombed the entire line of Albanian troops engaged in combat, achieving significant results. The Italian army claims that a team of General Seyum's troops attacked a detachment of soldiers 20 miles inside the Italian front line at night. Residents of the villages of Tabaga and Atbis assisted the soldiers in dispersing them, with only one Italian soldier injured. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Debono Returns to Rome: Prime Minister Personally Welcomes Him at the Train Station 14

(Rome) Former Commander-in-Chief of Italian Forces in East Africa, General Debono, arrived here today. A large crowd welcomed him. Mussolini and three thousand citizens greeted him at the station. Black Shirt comrades provided security at the station. The Speakers of both houses of parliament and other important figures were waiting on the platform. Today's welcoming atmosphere here is completely different from when General Debono arrived in Syracuse yesterday. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

Third Week of Economic Encirclement: Italian Corporate Council Meets; Mussolini Delivers Speech; Nationwide Gold Search to Resist Sanctions 15

(Rome) The Italian Chamber of Deputies (i.e., the Corporate Council) is scheduled to meet on Saturday this week. The only item on the agenda is "The Twentieth Day of Economic Encirclement" (Note: The League of Nations' sanctions against Italy began on November 18 and will reach twenty days on the 7th of this month). It is expected that Prime Minister Mussolini will deliver a speech at the meeting of the Chamber, outlining the military situation at the front and various plans to resist sanctions. Speaker Chiano (i.e., the father of the Prime Minister's son-in-law, Propaganda Minister Count Chiano) will report that forty-two members of the Chamber of Deputies have volunteered to go to East Africa to join the army and are therefore unable to attend. Finally, all members of the Chamber of Deputies will donate their gold medals to meet the needs of the national treasury. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

(Rome) In recent days, Italy has continued to collect gold throughout the country to replenish the reserves of the Bank of Italy. As for the embargo on oil, the general impression is that Britain will inevitably encounter real difficulties because other countries besides Britain may not be able to implement the embargo. Everyone believes in the government's propaganda, believing that even if there is an embargo on oil, Italy will be able to resist it. In addition, today's newspapers published news for the first time that Britain and France are now working hard to find a basis for peace talks that Italy can accept. The Forum newspaper requested, "Although there is no definitive evidence that British Foreign Secretary Sir El will come to Rome, this rumor proves that informal talks between Rome, Paris, and London must have made great progress." As for the British Mediterranean's largest warship, the Hood, and the Upper Noun, being transferred to the Atlantic Ocean, newspapers here also praised them. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

Italy Urgently Seeks to Break Through the Oil Embargo: Negotiations Established with US Standard Oil Company; Rome Denies, but French Media Speak Definitively 16

(Paris) The Paris Morning Post's Rome correspondent stated that Italy has established negotiations with the US New Jersey Standard Oil Company, agreeing that if Geneva passes an oil ban, the company will supply Italy with the oil it needs. If the Mediterranean is blocked, the oil needed by the Italian expeditionary force can be transported through the Far East to provide supplies. In return, the Italian government has granted the company a 30-year exclusive right to supply oil to the Italian government. Italy is also discussing a credit loan of 100 million gold lire with the company to develop oil fields in Albania. According to Italian government officials, Italy can obtain 300,000 tons of oil annually from this oil field. However, the Italian government has denied the above news. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

(New York) Secretary of State Hull recently announced to the press, "The State Department has not received any news to confirm the rumor that Mobil Oil Company has signed an oil sales contract with Italy." However, when reporters asked what attitude the US government would take if other companies signed such contracts, Hull declined to comment. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

Mobil Builds Oil Refinery in Italy 17

After Italy amended its tariff rules in 1933, the company weighed the pros and cons and then had a plan to build a factory, which was not initiated due to the oil embargo issue. US Neutrality Law: More Flexible Legislation Will Be a Major Issue in the Next Congress 18

More flexible neutrality legislation will be drafted, giving the President the power to declare a ban on the transportation of any goods beyond the normal amount to belligerent countries. (National Telegram, 5th)

British Foreign Secretary Explains Diplomatic Policy: Collective Action is Unwavering; Strive to Promote Italian-Albanian Peace Under Conditions That Do Not Humiliate Italy 19

(London) Foreign Secretary Ruhr delivered a long speech in the House of Commons last night, explaining the various aspects of British diplomatic policy, such as the disarmament issue, the redistribution of raw materials, the Far East issue, the Italian-Albanian dispute, and the Egyptian issue. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Attitude Towards the Italian-Albanian Case

The Foreign Secretary mentioned the Abyssinian issue, saying that Britain has fulfilled its full mission in collective action under the Covenant and continues to work to find a peaceful solution to the Italian-Albanian dispute. The member states of the League of Nations are almost entirely united, regardless of sacrifice, in participating in collective economic sanctions, and the member states are also unanimously in favor of the British and French efforts to seek peace. Britain and France have made it clear that (1) the scope of work is limited to the League of Nations, (2) they are willing to share special responsibilities with other member states as soon as possible, and (3) the conditions discussed must be acceptable to the League of Nations, Italy, and Albania. The League of Nations is currently carrying out economic sanctions, and the work is progressing smoothly. The situation is constantly under the supervision of the Committee of Experts. If gaps are found in the implementation, they will do everything possible to consolidate this common front.

Oil Embargo Issue

The Foreign Secretary also mentioned the oil embargo issue, saying that what I can say is that we have done our duty in the scope of the organization of collective action, and we are fully prepared to carry out our responsibilities in this oil embargo issue. The League of Nations has agreed in principle to the oil embargo. No country is more responsible for this collective decision than any other country. This is what I should declare. When the League of Nations collectively decides to implement the oil embargo, we are prepared to fulfill the collective action it has agreed upon. Recently, some people have pointed out that British oil companies are taking the opportunity to profit. I would like to explain this accusation. In the past quarter, the amount of oil imported into Italy has indeed increased significantly compared with the past, but the increase did not come from companies related to Britain. Taking the Anglo-Persian Oil Company as an example, the amount of oil it shipped to Italy in the first eleven months of this year was less than in the same period last year, and the decrease was particularly significant in the three months from August to October.

Acting in the Spirit of the League of Nations

The Foreign Secretary continued to mention the postponement of the meeting of the Eighteen-Nation Committee, saying that the change in the meeting date should not be regarded as the weakness of the member states' attitude, but only to give the opportunity to actively strive for a peaceful solution. It may be impossible to reconcile the differences between the League of Nations, Italy, and Albania, but Britain and France want to double their efforts in the short period before the League of Nations meeting. The world now urgently needs peace. Britain and France are acting for the League of Nations in the spirit of the League of Nations and are determined to make another major effort to seek peace. We do not want to humiliate Italy or weaken it. We very much hope to see Italy be a strong country in the world morally, politically, and socially, and be able to make great contributions to the world.

Appeal to Italy for Peace

I now appeal again to Mussolini and his countrymen to completely dispel any suspicion that Britain is harboring malice towards the League of Nations' assistance. We absolutely do not want to interfere in Italy's internal affairs. We sincerely hope to see Italy be strong and prosperous under the rule of a strong government in accordance with the political system desired by its people. When collective action is needed one day, the League of Nations, including Britain, is responsible for acting in accordance with the Covenant. The League of Nations will never be weak, and the member states will never fail to fulfill their obligations. The countries now need a long period of rest. If economic recovery is guaranteed, then permanent peace can be laid. The peace of Britain and its empire and the peace of the whole world are the basis of our policy. We will not hesitate to make our voice against war heard by everyone, and make our force against war felt by everyone. (Reuters dispatch)

French-Italian Relations with Egypt

Hall's speech also paid attention to recent events in Egypt, saying that the government does not express indifference to the emotions of the Egyptian people, and hopes to establish British-Egyptian relations on a satisfactory basis forever. The government is currently paying close attention to this. (National Telegram, 5th)

Sky Covenant Issue

The Foreign Secretary denied the rumor that the British government's diplomatic policy had changed after former Foreign Secretary Simon left office. He also said that the British government had tried to discuss the issue of reducing armaments with German leader Hitler again, but Germany currently holds the view that as long as the war in Albania is not over, continued discussions cannot achieve anything. The Sky Covenant and the reduction of sky armaments are all important plans today. The government will not neglect the opportunity to discuss again to obtain a satisfactory result.

Page 7

World Raw Material Distribution

The Foreign Secretary next mentioned the issue of raw materials in the colonies, reiterating his speech in Geneva, acknowledging the concerns of certain countries without raw materials, saying that he believed this issue was economic rather than political. The Foreign Secretary concluded that the government is prepared to conduct investigations in a tranquil atmosphere, but discussing this matter in the atmosphere of war cannot lead to any hope of a solution.

Eden Ends Debate

League of Nations Affairs Officer Eden concluded the debate on foreign affairs, saying that there are now fifty countries willing to bear the responsibility of unwelcome sanctions, which is excellent evidence that they are eager to see the birth of a new era. He believed that the increasing consolidation of the collective security system makes it possible to reduce the level of armaments. If the League of Nations' position is further stabilized by this dispute, it will create an opportunity to seek compromises on armament reduction and restrictions. We must not miss this opportunity. Then it was officially announced that the debate was postponed. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Berlin is Deeply Concerned

(Berlin) The political figures here are very concerned about the British Foreign Secretary Hall's diplomatic speech in the House of Commons last night. Among them, the one that concerns the Germans the most is the disarmament issue, especially the Sky Covenant issue. In well-informed circles, it is said that Leader Hitler has repeatedly stated in the past that Germany's army will not be allowed to modify its strength figures under any circumstances. However, he also said, "Regarding air force strength, if appropriate restrictions are added, I am also prepared to consider it, but the extent of the restrictions must be based on maintaining equality with the major Western European countries." (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Naval Conference Nears: Britain and the United States Will Jointly Put Pressure on Japan; Conflicting Negotiations Among Naval Powers Face Many Difficulties 20

(London) The London Naval Conference will officially open soon. Delegations from various participating countries have arrived one after another. The League of Nations has also sent observers to attend. The importance of this conference is evident. Since Japan announced the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty last December, the treaty's validity will expire at the end of next year, and the balance of power among the major naval powers created by the Washington Treaty will also collapse. Therefore, creating a new balance of power system among the major naval powers to replace the Washington system is the main goal of this naval conference. The mission of this naval conference is nothing more than two ends, namely the qualitative restriction and quantitative restriction of the navy. The difficulty in resolving these two problems lies in the mutual opposition of the naval powers. In the Pacific, there is the opposition of Britain, the United States, and Japan. In Europe, there is the opposition of France and Italy. This is in terms of all the difficulties in the past. Now, a new difficulty has been added, namely the German naval issue. Since Britain and Germany established a naval agreement on June 18 this year, the German naval power and the British naval power are linked to each other. In other words, if the British navy increases its tonnage, Germany will also increase accordingly. For this reason, the French navy must maintain constant contact with the British navy in order to deal with Germany. From now on, the French naval policy will depend on the British naval policy. If Britain expands its navy due to concerns about the Pacific, France will have to expand accordingly. In addition, on the surface, what is discussed at this naval conference is only limited to technical issues, but in practice, the advancement of naval negotiations will inevitably depend on political considerations. If the Washington Naval Treaty is to be re-discussed, then the military strategy clauses contained therein must also be studied. The provision in Article 19 of the Washington Naval Treaty prohibiting the increase of fortifications on Pacific islands is based on the naval balance of power in the Pacific at that time. Now that the naval balance of power has changed, this article needs to be revised. If the London Naval Conference fails to create a new balance of power system among the naval powers, then this article will have no possibility of continuing. Although the delegations from various countries attending the London Naval Conference have stated that they are prepared to discuss this issue, their attitudes are significantly different. Generally speaking, the Anglo-Saxon countries will jointly put pressure on Japan, while Japan hopes to maintain the current system of Pacific military strategy. This is almost inevitable. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

(Washington) Naval experts today believe that the United States will demand at the London Conference that any naval agreement must maintain the existing 5.5.3 ratio. If this conference fails to establish an agreement to limit naval armaments, the US naval authorities will seek funds to add warships, and regardless of how much other countries build, they must maintain this ratio. Before the current US fleet, in fact, it is not enough for the strength permitted by the London and Washington treaties. Although large-scale construction has been carried out in recent years, it will not be able to achieve this goal for all classes of warships until six years after the expiration of the two treaties, that is, before 1942. The US naval authorities have also noticed that aviation power is increasingly eroding national defense. The Navy Department has been working hard to implement a plan to increase air force strength, and Congress has also passed it. The Director of the Aviation Office of the Navy Department, Jin Shi, officially announced that the department has built 59 large bombers and has ordered a large number of high-speed and powerful pursuit and reconnaissance aircraft. Although the naval authorities are unwilling to increase the burden on taxpayers due to the international arms race, if other naval powers expand the construction program, the United States must do its best to follow suit for the sake of national security. (National Telegram, 5th)

(London) The 1933 Strong Warrior Battleship Yearbook was published today, stating that no matter what the outcome of the Qing Dynasty Conference, the world has already fallen into a new era of building capital ships. However, it has not been confirmed that Japanese submarines are equipped with small aircraft, and it is said that 1936 to 1937 will be a prosperous year for naval construction. (National Telegram, 6th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Disarmament Representative Nagano held a meeting with foreign journalists on the 4th to explain Japan's disarmament policy. When talking about abolishing submarines, he also vaguely revealed Japan's intention to discuss political issues such as the Pacific defense restriction agreement. After seeing this news telegram, the Japanese naval authorities claimed that this conversation completely contradicted Japan's fundamental principles, and on the 5th, they asked the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to inquire about the truth. Artistic Musings

The Face of the Clock (Part 1) 33

— Feng Zikai

Once, while sitting on a Shanghai streetcar, I happened to catch a glimpse of a tall building outside the window, and I saw a large clock installed on it. Its form was quite eye-catching, in a novel way. The impression I got at that glance was unusually fresh, like seeing a country girl with thick eyebrows and big eyes after being used to seeing urban ladies with delicate features and slender eyes. This sparked various thoughts in me while I was on the car, and I still haven't forgotten it, so I'm writing down that whimsical thought now.

I remember seeing illustrations of clocks of this type in foreign books discussing "new art." The clocks don't use Roman numerals or Arabic numerals to indicate the hours, but only draw twelve thick, short straight lines, all looking like 1 o'clock. But this was the first time I'd seen a real one in China. The first thing I thought when I saw it was its connection to my personal past: about ten years ago, when I was a teacher at a school, I suddenly found the face of the clock I was used to looking at annoying. Because some of the twelve Arabic numerals seemed to urge me to go to class, some seemed to order me to sleep, some seemed to force me to get up, and some seemed to shout at me to hurry up and catch the streetcar, making me uncomfortable even on holidays. So I took out my oil painting tools, used Cobalt to paint over the entire clock face and hands, and used other colors to draw a part of a willow tree in the upper right corner, hanging down a few willow branches. Then I cut two swallows out of black paper and glued them to the tips of the hands. In this way, my clock looked like a miniature painting in a round frame. Sometimes, when the hands were in the right place, the clock face would display a very pleasing composition. As for practical use, I only needed to recognize that the vertical was 12 or 6 o'clock, and the horizontal was 3 or 9 o'clock, and I could estimate the other times by eye within each 90-degree angle. I was very pleased with this gadget and even duplicated it on the wall clock, turning it into an oil painting. (This was recorded in my Green Edge Hall Notes.) That wall clock is still hanging on the east wall of my home in my hometown. However, I later disliked it again and had already painted over the willows and swallows, now only leaving a white face and two black hands. My family and I had become accustomed to the "wordless clock," and no one asked to add Arabic numerals. Frequent guests were no longer surprised and could even read the time. Several children with sharp eyes could even tell the exact time, down to the minute and half-minute. Because of this past connection, I was particularly concerned about the transformations of clock faces. Seeing that "new art" style clock from the streetcar window that day caught my attention. But now I bring this up not to prove my prescience about "new art" forms. The aforementioned gadget was entirely out of my curiosity and playfulness and had nothing to do with art. It's just that the point of not writing numbers on the clock face coincides with my old experience, so I'm bringing it up again. Now, I think calmly: My method—drawing willows and swallows or painting on the clock face—was too curious at the time, only suitable for my own enjoyment and not worth imitating by others. But as advocated by the new art, I feel that the matter of eliminating Arabic numerals from clock faces is worth discussing, and I might as well chat about it here.

Page 8

South China Japanese Consuls Hold Meeting in Hong Kong 60

Taiwan's Foreign Affairs Section Chief Also Participates, Emphasizing the Development of Commerce and Protection of Overseas Chinese

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, diplomatic winds and clouds have been urgent, and the North China issue is becoming increasingly serious. Japanese consuls in various parts of southern China, in order to cope with the current situation, decide on a unified policy, and discuss the development of local commerce and transportation, gathered in Hong Kong on November 30 to hold a South China Japanese Consul Conference. Participants included Japanese Consul in Hong Kong, Mizusawa Kosaku; Japanese Consul in Guangdong, Kawai Tatsuo; Japanese Consul in Fuzhou, Nakamura Toyoichi; Japanese Consul in Xiamen, Yamada Yoshiotaro; Japanese Consul in Shantou, Harada Chuichi; and Sakamoto, the Chief of the Foreign Affairs Section of Taiwan, who arrived in Hong Kong on the morning of the 29th aboard the Guangdong Maru to prepare to participate. Sakamoto previously served as the Chief of the Third Commerce Section of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and was assigned to Taiwan in February of this year to serve as the Chief of the Taiwan Foreign Affairs Section. He is not only responsible for all foreign affairs in Taiwan but also serves as an official in the South China Consulate and is a trustee of the Hong Kong Consulate. His mission in participating in the Hong Kong South China Japanese Consul Conference is of great significance. On the 29th, the Japanese Consul in Hong Kong hosted a reception for the consuls at his office to exchange views. According to Okuda Otsujiro, the secretary of the Hong Kong Consulate, this conference is a regular event for South China consuls and has little to do with the North China incident. In this era of economic recession, the South China consuls should convene a meeting to develop commerce and decide on an overall strategy to facilitate progress. Japanese businessmen in Hong Kong were also invited to participate in the meeting, which lasted about three days. The following are the matters that can be published at the meeting: 1. Each consul reports on the local situation. 2. Measures against anti-Japanese sentiment. 3. Discussing methods of communication between consulates in various places. 4. Matters concerning Japanese crew members. 5. Promoting trade and developing commerce. 6. Issues concerning the protection of Japanese ships. 7. Issues concerning the protection of Japanese nationals. After the meeting on the 30th, Mizusawa Kosaku, the Japanese Consul in Hong Kong, hosted a reception for Chinese and Western journalists at the Japanese Club at 5 PM to report on the progress of the meeting. It is also reported that Japan will set up a communications headquarters in Guangdong, on the one hand, to be well-informed about news in South China, and on the other hand, to communicate South China's sentiments and adopt a policy of distant alliances. (December 1)

Chaoshan Strictly Suppresses Smuggling 61

More than 20 Branch Posts are Set Up Along the Coast, and Provincial Supervisors are Dispatched to Preside

Shantou Correspondence: There are many smuggled goods imported in the Chaoshan area. The military and police authorities announced a unified land and water anti-smuggling operation on November 1st. The province has dispatched two additional tax squadrons, ten special agents, and five anti-smuggling warships. More than 20 branch posts have been set up along the coast of Chaoshan. Xiao Sheng, the Director of the Chaoshan Anti-Smuggling Division, has been hesitant to comply due to the importance of the matter. The province has dispatched Fan Zhanpeng to Shantou to take charge. The form of the inland anti-smuggling branch posts is equivalent to the former customs and likin bureaus. If goods that have already paid special taxes and special levies are shipped, a certificate from the Agricultural Tax Bureau must be obtained to prove the origin of the goods, which must be presented to the branch post for inspection and release. The merchant who buys the goods at the same time must also be responsible for signing. When the goods are transported to their destination, they must still be deregistered. This is to prevent smugglers from undermining the revenue from special taxes. The province has recently dispatched anti-smuggling supervisors and special agents to Shantou, all of whom are responsible for establishing branch posts. It is said that with strict anti-smuggling measures, the activities of traitors will be effectively prevented.

Songjiang: Framing Someone for Drug Trafficking is Exposed 62

Yao Jinrong, a villager in Chedun Township, and his wife, Zhao Meiyuan, are the lovers of Wang Shuqin, who runs a teahouse. After the divorce, they lived together. Wang had a grudge against Yao. A few days ago, provincial inspectors seized two cans of red pills at Yao Jinrong's house, with a note with Yao's name on them. They were hidden under a broken bridge in the public access street outside Yao's room. The people and the evidence were sent to the county government for interrogation. Yao protested his innocence. After a rigorous investigation by Officer Zhang, it was learned that the case was a frame-up. It was indeed a conspiracy between Wang Duqin and Shen Huisheng. They sent Ye Maosheng to arrest them. Ye Maosheng and Shen Huisheng were arrested and interrogated. They both confessed the truth. They claimed that Wang Shen and Yu had a grudge, so they ordered them to come up with 16 yuan and buy a can of red pills from Hua Ti and divide them into two cans. After affixing the notes, Shen went to set them up and then reported to the Provincial Inspection Association, which sent companions to arrest them. The county government ordered them to be detained. Wang Shuqin pawned the teahouse to someone and left Songjiang with his family after the case, showing that he was fleeing in fear of punishment. The police are now dispatched to pursue him.

Wuxi: Strange News of a Resurrected Dead Person Spreads 64

In the Beiqiao area of the third district of Xiyi, it has recently been rumored that a certain surname died at the age of sixteen. After eight years, his parents called him back to life this spring. Last month, he was planting wheat in the fields. As for the method of resurrecting the dead, one hundred copper coins must be collected from one hundred families with the same surname, and one hundred soy beans must be placed in the coin holes, arranged in the shape of a human on the dead person's coffin, and incense and candles must be burned. The parents or children of the deceased must call the deceased's name next to the tomb at 2:00 AM, noon, and evening every day, one hundred times each time. Each time they call, the dead person will grow muscles on four limbs, and after calling for ninety-seven forty-nine days, the dead person's body will be completely formed and resurrected. Ordinary men and women are running around telling each other, causing a great wave of imitation. Residents such as Huang Dabao of Zhang Jingqiao Cai Lane and various villages such as Caozhuangli, Tangguan Port, and Sifang Bridge, as well as the Liu surname at the foot of the North Licheng and the Fan surname at Yanqiao in the urban area, have taken such actions. In fact, this is absurd and baseless, and the matter is superstitious. It is also rumored that a living Bao Gong has been found in Changzhou, who can cure all diseases, which has been widely spread. Teahouses and taverns are using it as a topic of conversation. It is hoped that the authorities will strictly ban it.

Changzhou Remodeling Roads and Demolishing Houses 65

The new road outside Zhongshan Gate in Wuyi County is an important route to the railway station and connecting various highways. It has been in disrepair for years, is rugged and uneven, and the road is narrow, causing congestion for vehicles and pedestrians. Remodeling is urgently needed. The county government submitted a request to the Construction and Finance Departments to widen the road surface to 16 meters. The departments approved an appropriation of 7,500 yuan from the construction funds for this year's projects. The county government has received orders to immediately announce to residents on both sides of Xinfeng Street that they must demolish their houses according to regulations within one month to allow for the 16-meter width. Those who fail to demolish their houses by the deadline will be forced to do so to facilitate traffic and create a grand spectacle. The road surface project will be contracted out through bidding once the houses are demolished. Construction will begin immediately after the demolition is completed.

Yangzhou Forging Bank of China Receipts Leads to Arrest 67

At 3:30 PM on the 4th, a villager named Tao Youcai, wearing a gray long gown and a black melon-shaped hat, came to the Yangzhou branch of the Bank of China with a receipt for the 16th issue of the Aviation Lottery. The receipt stated, "Received today the first prize of the 16th Aviation Lottery, No. 11168, Article 3, prize money totaling 21,000 silver dollars. This lottery ticket should be submitted to the Aviation Office for verification. This amount was paid on the 2nd of April with a receipt. Respectfully, Shi Xiansheng, Wu Zhao. Signed, Bank of China Yangzhou Branch, through 11.16." The receipt had a seal on the left side. The bank staff suspected it was a forgery. They reported it to the police, and Chen Zhaoxuan, a policeman, took the person and the receipt to the First Precinct. A photograph of the forged receipt was taken and filed. Yang, an inspector from the precinct, interrogated Tao Youcai, who confessed that he was 41 years old, a farmer from Shaobo. He came to Yangzhou at 2 PM. The receipt was given to him by his nephew, Shi Yiding, who lives in Qiaoshu and is currently residing with Xu Xiangsheng in the northern suburbs. Shi asked him to check the number first, and Shi planned to come to town on the 7th to collect the money. Unexpectedly, the receipt was fake, and he was arrested. That evening, around 8 PM, the person and the confession were handed over to the Public Security Bureau for further action.

Siyang Many Drown in Ferry Capsizing at Shiji 69

Except for a few who were rescued, about 30 people drowned. That day was the market day in Shiji. When the news spread, the relatives of the deceased, both men and women, went to the ferry to search for the bodies and hired people to salvage them from the river.

Local News

Li Yingcong Proposes Gliding Sport, Seeking National Leaders as Sponsors, Starting a Gliding Study Group in Shanghai 70

Mr. Li Jingcong, General Manager of Eurasia Aviation Corporation, believes that gliding is popular in Europe, America, and Japan. This sport is not only the most noble game for young people to temper their bodies and minds but also has the function of preliminary flight training. Therefore, he feels it is necessary to promote it. He is currently seeking national leaders to co-sponsor the initiative and plans to first organize a Gliding Study General Association in Shanghai, and then establish branches in various regions. Central News Agency reporters, believing that this matter is of great importance and will be of interest to the public, visited Mr. Li yesterday. He said: "Gliding has a history of more than 20 years. Initially, it shared the same flight ideals as aviation. Aviation has progressed from lighter-than-air airships to today's heavier-than-air airplanes. Gliding has also gone its own way, with continuous research. Progress has been especially rapid since the European War. Currently, it is not only popular in various European and American countries, but also in neighboring Japan, where they are sparing no effort to promote it. Gliding means traveling in the sky using a glider without relying on engine power or the buoyancy of gasbags. The ascent method can be either by towing with a car, releasing with a winch, or gliding down from a high slope. Then, the pilot naturally rises with the air, manipulating the tail to continue forward, circling, or ascending. The latest record shows that gliding can reach as high as 4,500 meters, travel as far as 500 kilometers, and last for 36 and a half hours. This is a human instinct that has been developed and realized today, which is not surprising. Gliding can be regarded as a form of entertainment, but it is actually a most advanced sport. Sports were initially limited to good days in spring and autumn, with track and field, ball games, and wrestling as the main events. In the past decade, winter skating and summer swimming have become popular, which, in addition to tempering the body and mind, also implies competition with nature on a flat surface. This is progress in sports, but gliding is not limited to seasons, and its significance of competing with the atmosphere is advanced from a flat surface to a three-dimensional one. Therefore, its progress is above all other sports. Moreover, the operation of a glider involves using its tail to adapt to the turbulence of the airflow, which is the same principle as engine flight. Therefore, it can be regarded as preliminary training for engine flight. However, the lowest-priced engine-powered airplane costs more than tens of thousands of dollars, and there are also large amounts of fuel and depreciation costs during flight. A glider may cost less than a thousand dollars, and there are no costs during use. Therefore, gliding is a good way to promote the aviation industry. I believe that gliding is of great significance. Therefore, I plan to invite several national leaders and military and political authorities to initiate and promote it. I plan to first organize a Gliding Study General Association in Shanghai, recruit members, and manufacture gliders and train gliding skills at Longhua Airport. In the future, I also plan to promote it in the interior. If it can be realized as soon as possible, I hope that aspiring young people will actively participate, which will be a blessing for the future of the country and the nation."

Requires Approval from the Ministry Before Proceeding, General Manager Dai Enji Has Returned to Shanghai

Finnish Officials and Residents in Shanghai Celebrate Independence Day 72

Acting Consul General Hosts Reception for Residents Last Night, Lectures on Sino-Finnish Relations Broadcast in Chinese

Yesterday was the 18th anniversary of Finland's declaration of complete independence. Finnish officials and residents in Shanghai took a holiday to celebrate. The acting Finnish Consul General in Shanghai, Max Nygren, hosted a reception for Finnish residents at the consulate on Muirhead Road at 8 PM. At 7:30 PM, a Chinese staff member was sent to deliver a radio address in Chinese about Finland's founding and Sino-Finnish relations. Also, the 15th of this month is the 74th birthday of Pehr Evind Svinhufvud, the founding father of Finland and the current President.

Dalu Daily reports that the Nordic country of Finland celebrated its 18th anniversary of independence yesterday (the 6th). Finland has an area of 149,900 square miles and a population of 3.8 million. After separating from Sweden in 1809, it became a semi-independent Grand Duchy under the Russian Empire, with its own government and parliament, and its own currency, enjoying an independent economic life. In 1905, the old four-chamber parliament was merged into a single-chamber parliament, granting women the same social rights as men. In 1917, it declared complete independence. The country's fortunes are improving daily, repairing domestic affairs, strengthening diplomatic relations, and focusing on absolute neutrality in the face of aggregations of special political interests in foreign policy. In a time of national crisis and economic hardship, Finland has been able to weather the storm peacefully. The current coalition government was formed in the winter of 1932. A general election was held during its term. Its President, Pehr Evind Svinhufvud, is a veteran of Finnish politics. Although he is 74 years old, he is still energetic and is known as "Old Peter" in the country. Finland's relations with China are very cordial. In 1926, it was the first country to sign a treaty of friendship with China and voluntarily abolished consular jurisdiction. Today, Finnish newspapers express sincere sympathy and understanding for China's difficulties.

After Hong Kong Stabilizes Foreign Exchange, Exchange Rate Between Shanghai and Hong Kong Balances 79

Central Bank Announces Foreign Exchange Market Prices Yesterday, 100 National Currency Equals 90.5 Hong Kong Dollars

The Hong Kong government issued an order on the 5th to nationalize privately held silver dollars, and all transactions are limited to legal tender and banknotes from HSBC, Chartered Bank, and Mercantile Bank. It also established a Foreign Exchange Reserve Committee to adjust the exchange rate of the Hong Kong dollar. According to a reporter from New Voices News Agency, banking circles revealed that the Hong Kong government's move is a policy to prevent speculators from harming the interests of legal trade. Therefore, the prices for the purchase and sale of exchange funds and bills of exchange will not be announced to prevent speculators from operating. As for balancing foreign exchange in China, it is not only has no impact, but may even be beneficial. It is hoped that the price of telegraphic transfers of national currency against Hong Kong dollars can be suppressed. The exchange rate announced by the Central Bank this morning (6th) of 100 national currency equaling 90.5 Hong Kong dollars is proof of this. In the past, 100 national currency only equaled about 70 Hong Kong dollars, a difference of 20 to 30 dollars. It is hoped that this loss can be avoided in the future.

Ministry of Finance Stipulates Regulations for Foreign Banks to Receive Legal Tender 85

60% in Cash, 40% in Reserves Exchanged with Three Banks, Mercantile, Citibank, and Other Banks Have Agreed to Comply

New Voices News Agency reports that after the Shanghai Foreign Exchange Banks Association submitted its opinions to Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi on paying in silver and exchanging it for legal tender, the Ministry of Finance has replied, agreeing to exchange legal tender for 60% in cash and 40% in reserves with the Central, China, and Communications Banks. The details are as follows:

Ministry of Finance Responds, Exchange Methods

Kirkhope, Chairman of the Foreign Exchange Banks Association and Managing Director of Mercantile Bank, and Yabuki Keiichi, a member of the committee and Managing Director of Yokohama Specie Bank, visited Minister of Finance Kong Xianxi and contributed their opinions on paying in silver and exchanging it for legal tender. A reporter from New Voices News Agency learned from banking circles yesterday that the Ministry of Finance has replied, agreeing to follow the methods for Chinese banks and money shops, exchanging legal tender for 60% in cash and 40% in reserves with the Central, China, and Communications Banks.

Foreign Banks Have Agreed to Comply

The Banks Association held another meeting the night before last, attended by 20 banks including Mercantile, HSBC, Yokohama Specie, Citibank, and Mitsui. Chairman Kirkhope first reported on the progress of the Ministry of Finance's reply. It is heard that Mercantile, HSBC, Citibank, Banque de l'Indochine, American Express, Banca Andreasi, Banca Italiana per la Cina, Deutsch-Asiatische Bank, British Bank for Foreign Trade, Banque Franco-Chinoise, Banque Belge pour l'Etranger, Chase Bank, and other banks have agreed to comply. It is heard that Japanese banks have also replied, but it needs further negotiation before it can be decided.

After checking the organization and uniform styles of the Society's rescue teams, which have been approved by the Ministry, three lines of detailed drawings are hereby issued for compliance. (1) Style: Zhongshan suit. (2) Color: Summer uses straw yellow, domestic serge or twill fabric; winter uses khaki, domestic wool fabric; servants use black and blue domestic fabric in winter and summer. (3) Armband: A white armband with a red cross is worn on the upper left arm, according to the Geneva Convention, it should be stamped by a senior military officer. (4) Cap badge: Military style cap, the cap badge uses the national emblem of the blue sky and white sun, 3.5 cm in diameter. (5) Hat sleeve gold thread: The president and vice president of the general association have three broad lines, directors and supervisors have two broad and one narrow, team leaders and deputy team leaders have one broad and one narrow, and other members have one broad. The president and vice president of the branch association have one broad and one narrow line, directors and supervisors have two narrow lines, team leaders and deputy team leaders have one broad line, and other members have one narrow line. The width of the broad line is 1 cm, and the narrow line is 5 mm. (6) Collar badge: A white circle with a red cross, 2.5 cm in diameter. (7) Symbol: White silk cloth, 9 cm wide and 5 cm long, green border for team members and staff, servants are not colored. The president's small seal is stamped in the center and sewn directly above the left pocket.

The 13th Inauguration of the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union Executive and Supervisory Committee 88

Yesterday, a declaration of inauguration was issued, revealing four major guidelines.

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union held the swearing-in ceremony for its 13th Executive and Supervisory Committee at 2:00 PM yesterday in the auditorium on the third floor of the Shanghai Postal Administration. 135 representatives from various branches, all members of the Executive and Supervisory Committee, representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters Lu Yinchu, and representatives from the National Postal Workers' General Union Lu Jingshi and Zhu Xuefan were present. Zhang Yidao, Shui Xiangyun, and Fan Caicong were nominated as the presidium. First, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that the current Executive and Supervisory Committee was holding the inauguration ceremony today, deeply aware of the perilous situation of the country and the nation, and deeply aware of the heavy responsibility of the committee members. Therefore, in addition to seeking the development of postal services and the welfare of members, it is necessary to strengthen forces and strive for the survival of the country and the nation. Then, Lu Yinchu, a representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, delivered a training speech, stating that the glorious history and sound organization of the union in the past only inspire admiration and praise. It is hoped that in the future, the union will stand on the national front and continue to work hard. Finally, Lu Jingshi and Zhu Xuefan, representatives of the National Postal Workers' General Union, delivered training speeches one after another, with many exhortations. After the speech, a declaration was issued and a photo was taken before the meeting adjourned. The following is an excerpt of the inauguration declaration: "The Supervisory Committee of this newspaper, etc., resolved to formally swear in on December 6, sincerely acknowledging the importance of the trust placed by the union and the earnest expectations of society. We will certainly devote our foolish sincerity and bear this arduous task. The changes in the world are severe, and our fear increases. We dare not fail to continue the spirit of past struggles and encourage future progress. Therefore, we hereby reveal our innermost thoughts and announce our guidelines as follows: First, the thorough implementation of the spirit of service. Our postal workers' service has always taken benefiting the country and society as the premise. At this time of international turbulence and frequent domestic disasters, looking around, we are more determined in our ambition. We sincerely hope to work harder and strive together with people from all walks of life to turn the tide in the middle of the stream and promote the revival of the country. Postal service is one of the transportation industries, and what it concerns is of utmost importance to the national economy and the people's livelihood. Our postal workers dedicate themselves to it. How cautious, motivated, dedicated, and committed should we be in order to seek the development of the postal service's future? Three days to maintain the postal system. The perfection of postal services has always been praised by people from all walks of life. The reason for this is that it relies on a sound and good system. However, as time passes and circumstances change, those who take the opportunity to destroy it emerge one after another. Our postal workers strive to protect the postal service for the sake of the postal service and for their own sake. The past traces of protecting the postal service are still clearly visible. In the future, we should continue this spirit and implement our original intentions. If anyone attempts to undermine our sound and good postal system of more than ten years, we will regard them as public enemies and vow to do everything in our power to deal with them, even if it means going through fire and water. Three days to consolidate the internal organization. This union has gone through many difficulties to achieve what it is today. This long and glorious history is all the result of long-term struggle. However, there are still many obstacles and dangers have not been subdued. In the future, we should consolidate our front and unify our steps to fight against the harsh environment. All our members, under the leadership of the National Postal Workers' General Union, must unite in good faith, fully support, strictly abide by discipline, and obey orders in order to strengthen the entire force and consolidate a permanent foundation. Fourth, to increase the welfare of members. The greatest mission of this union internally is to strive for the welfare of members. Relying on the efforts of past committees and the supervision of all members, considerable achievements have been made. In the future, we should actively carry out our work to satisfy the expectations of members. Everything from the growth of intelligence, the improvement of life, and the expansion of careers must be planned and promoted to be realized. Uphold the purpose of mutual assistance and use the strength of collective efforts, without pursuing empty talk or being biased, so that all members can enjoy the rights they deserve. The above four points are the entire guidelines for the future efforts of this union. We will certainly follow this goal, move forward bravely, and work hard to live up to the heavy trust placed by the two members and the earnest expectations of society. This is our declaration, December 6, 24th year."

Illegal Collection of Taxes: People Can Sue the Government 93

The Guomin News Agency said that the Ministry of Finance's interpretation of the measures to punish illegal re-levies of abolished taxes and miscellaneous levies is as follows: All abolished taxes and miscellaneous levies that have not been included in the local budget are illegal levies collected outside the law. They should be handled in accordance with the public decree of the National Government on the implementation of local budgets and punished in accordance with Article 129 of the Criminal Code. When the re-levy begins, the people have no obligation to pay and may sue the superior government.

The Price of Kailan Coal Soars: The Coal Industry Association Convenes a Meeting to Stabilize Coal Prices 96

The Shanghai Coal Industry Association, due to the soaring price of Kailan coal, convened an emergency joint meeting of the Executive, Supervisory, and Evaluation Committees at 2:30 PM yesterday. More than 20 committee members, including Bao Zhexing, Chen Yushu, Xu Yiyong, Mao Chunpu, Wang Wenzheng, and Chen Weibin, attended. Chen Yushu, the chairman, reported that the price of Kailan coal had risen twice for no reason in the past three weeks. Lump coal rose from $10.10 per ton to $13, and small coal rose from $8.80 to $11. Especially this afternoon, small coal in the market rose by $1.40 per ton and lump coal rose by $0.50, which agitated the market and affected the price of coal. The meeting decided to publicly nominate Bao Zhexing, Mao Chunpu, Wang Wenzheng, Chen Guanggen, Wang Qinfei, Wang Ziyuan, Zhang Bokun, and Chen Yushu to negotiate with the Kailan Sales Office to discuss stabilizing coal prices in order to stabilize the market.

The Tram Company Demarcates the Price of Currency from Yesterday: $1 Legal Tender for 3,000 Wen 97

With the implementation of the new currency, the Shanghai Tram Company once stipulated that each dollar of legal tender could be exchanged for 2,900 copper coins. Now, it has been recently decided that each dollar of legal tender will be 3,000 Wen, which is in line with the regulations of the Ministry of Finance. Fifty cents of subsidiary currency will be 1,500 Wen, 25 cents will be 750 Wen, 20 cents of subsidiary notes will be 600 Wen, 10 cents of subsidiary currency will be 300 Wen, and Shuanghao will be 500 Wen. French Concession trams and buses have also been using the same rates since yesterday. However, the exchange rate in general cigarette and paper shops is only about 2,970 per dollar of legal tender, while Shuangjiao is only about 280 per 10 cents, and Shuanghao can be exchanged for 510, with a discount of 290 to 300.

One of the Scenic Spots in Southeast China: The New Construction of Yixing Shanjuan Cave is Completed 100

The completion ceremony will be held on the 10th of this month.

Yixing Shanjuan Cave is one of the scenic spots in Southeast China. Recently, it has been renovated under the direction of Mr. Chu Nanqiang, a local squire. The upper, middle, and lower levels are connected into one, and all can be passed through. Outside the cave, the flying waterfall faces the door, like a white silk. The completion ceremony will be held on December 10, and it will be open for permanent tours. The Municipal Bureau of Public Works Cleans Up the Accumulated Silt on the Banks of the Suzhou Creek 101

The Suzhou Creek, a key waterway in Shanghai, has been silted up for many years, making the river narrow. The congestion of ships causes great difficulties in water transport. Since the Wusong River Conservancy Committee and the Shanghai Bureau of Public Works began to carry out dredging work in sections, the section from Laozha to Beixinjing has been completed, and the work from Yujidun to Jiwangmiao has also been underway for a long time. Now that winter has arrived, the tides are low and the water is shallow. There is still a large amount of silt that was piled up on the north and south banks, below the river banks and river bends of Fanwangdu, Caojiadu, and Xiaoshadu during dredging. It has not yet been removed, which is very inconvenient for ship traffic. Starting yesterday, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works dispatched a large number of workers to transport the accumulated silt to ships and vehicles for land and water transportation to other places to facilitate water transport.
